O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science along with its fulfillment, and I have made an end through its explanations and by its revelations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is hidden from all, so it has been lost and neglected; only a few brief references to it remain in the books of ancient authors who have described this work with their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity; intentions have become closed off, and knowledge has been pushed aside.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Or it seems to me that I wish to revive it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and explanation, and of abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And then will come the forms of the cautery irons, and of other instruments for the work with their adjustment as well as an explanation of its preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine has become elongated.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for whoever undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of limbs and their shapes, connections and separations; be aware of bones, nerves, veins and arteries, and have knowledge of the numbers and movements of them all.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the name along with the noun is much, and with work it becomes little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should take care not to fall into error or harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus, I have seen many who involve themselves in this science, abandoning it without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he cut her carotid arteries.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Which caused so much blood to come out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another doctor treating a stone in an old man's bladder, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	He carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the old man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another doctor treating a duke of our land who had a broken leg with an open fracture wound.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	And the ignorant surgeon restrains the fracture on top of the wound with bandages tied too tightly, leaving no room for the wound to drain, and thus he leaves it untreated.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commands that it must not be untied.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And so it was delayed, causing the leg to swell entirely and the foot to become damaged, leading to its ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called upon to attend him, and I hurried to come and release his leg.
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I released it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	However, the damage to his limb had already taken hold, and I could not cure him.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And the corruption kept spreading through the limb until it was all lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And then I saw another marvel which aggravated an abscess, and then it inflamed due to the wickedness of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer, when it is caused by melancholic humor, it should not be treated with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corrupted matter can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this, my dear son, you must understand that manual work is divided into two categories:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I shall demonstrate in each place of this book where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	This is why you must be cautious so that the foolish surgeon does not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take up your tools carefully, approach your patients gently yet firmly, and employ the best methods so that by God's grace you achieve success and are praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	And leave behind terrifying illnesses of serious illness;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Remove your weapons from whatever makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you can travel from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake the treatment of any serious illness unless you are called upon as a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauterization and other medical treatments for acute diseases, and the chapters are arranged from head to toe.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	And the shapes of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and everything else that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping, wounds, arrow extractions, and similar matters.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And this chapter sets out the order of operations and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and related matters.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it sets out the order from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we embark on this work, it is necessary for me to explain the qualities of remedies and their potential harm according to each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of healing, and their hindrance, are a long speech and subtle science, and hidden secrets.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And many wise men have spoken of this, and agreed upon it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And their words suffice for little to me, because I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery universally helps all constitutions where there is matter, except for two constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	That is to say, a hot constitution without matter, and a dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry constitution with matter, some argued and said that cautery is of great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That cautery is not beneficial for illnesses that arise from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And he who says otherwise, claims that cautery provides great relief to hot and dry ailments that arise within the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body of a man to fire in terms of moisture and complexion, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	But in any case, do not rely solely on the opinion of someone who has experienced it, but rather on that of an expert who understands through long practice the chapter on cauterization, and the variety of human constitutions, as well as their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and how they arise over time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We need not fear for other constitutions, especially in the case of cold and moist ailments.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed on the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that fire together with cauterization is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come forth unless to the member that is cooked, and it harms no other member if left alone.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning remedies spread from one member to another, leading to diseases that require prompt treatment.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And sometimes the patient may even die as a result.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fires due to their height and the goodness of their substance do not harm, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experimentation and the length of my service and study in this art, and it is based on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this I excuse myself for the length of my words, as I do not wish to take away from you the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of its work, how it begins to heal illnesses of the body, just as the philosopher says when demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done, choosing careful timing.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, for the harmful things arising from below can be removed by the help of cauterization.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially if the cauterization is necessary for pain, it must be done quickly to prevent further serious harm from coming to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	and never think of doing it like foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it like this;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they believe, because cauterization is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries out the humors causing the pain; it is more powerful than any other medicine due to its speed of action, and for the strength of its work and its mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is remarkable that the disease may sometimes come according to the patient's complexion, the location of the disease and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered in it the excesses due to the consumption of meat and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered where there is little excess and moisture, such as dental cauterization for pain, and similar things, and this type of pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort in medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterizations are valuable after medicinal treatments, but their understanding is false, and cauterization is the last resort in medicine because when we administer various treatment methods for any illness, and they prove ineffective, then we use cauterization, which works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauterizations with a golden instrument are more beneficial than those of iron, and they attributed this to the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the place of cauterization does not cause inflammation, but this is not always true as I have tested it myself and found that it occurs in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And gold cauterizations are more beneficial than those of iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	However, when you heat a golden instrument, you cannot tell when it is hot by its colour and it cools down quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	And if one heats it too much.
si font au feu;	They are done by fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we use fire cauterization, which we have adapted to fit our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter on the head to foot so that it might be easier for you to find your way through it.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cauterization.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is effective for moisture and coldness in the brain, and there are two ways to perform it due to a disease called 'soda', and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, causing multiple symptoms like dreams, toothaches, sore throat, and especially all diseases stemming from cold such as paralysis, sodas, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine, modifying the head three or four times, according to what the virtues, moisture, and habit of the patient can endure.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	And then make the patient's head sweat again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit with crossed arms between your hands, and place his hands on your shoulders.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Afterwards, place the root of your palm at the root of their nose between their two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And where your two thumbs will come, bleed then heat the cautery called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on an ink-marked spot, then move your hand gently downward and inward in a twisting manner.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift your hand slightly, and reposition it if you see the bone moving even a little bit.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you don't see it moving, restart the cauterization until you see the bone as I've told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Afterward, take some softened silk and put it in a pile of soft cotton, then place this on the spot for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Then apply moistened cotton mixed with butter over it.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Leave it in place until the burning sensation has gone.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the wound with the remedy known as "tetrafarmacon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges itself.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, aid is provided.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one must leave the cautery in place until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it shall be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one must leave the cautery on so long and press it with such force that it pierces the bone as wide as the "vertuil" that women put in their sleeves, because this allows the humours to escape more easily.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	Afterwards, it should be treated and sutured.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two types of cauterization do not seem to me to be good at all in every way, except for some people where there is a sense of fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the bone is weakened by the constant movement of nature, as we witness in other limbs.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	Even when the bone of the patient is weak by nature, and the first type of cauterization seems more effective and useful to me, I employ it together with these treatments for a cure.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When a patient experiences chronic head pain that persists for an extended period, they should use herbs and pills known as "cochie," along with purgatives, oils, and poultices.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	For if you perform the cautery as we have described before, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take heed if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution, and ensure it is not too cold.
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then cauterize below the aforementioned cautery site slightly.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards, cauterize each corner of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and perform a cautery where it is called "the vessel".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	And there is a place for the application of cups.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	Adjust your hand so that you do not see down to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The sick person feels much greater pain with this cautery than with others, and I will speak about that later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is fitting that the cauterizations of the horns are more subtle than those used for cauterizing the middle part of the head, and this is the procedure:
dou cautere dou chief	For the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head, and the disease extends to the eye, and the skull has been cleansed with purifying medicines, and other treatments that I have mentioned for dividing diseases have been applied, yet none of these provide relief:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then treat it with two types of cauterization, namely medical cautery and fire cautery.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	Medical cauterization involves taking a piece of alum, removing the bark and cutting it into two pieces for the skull bones, then making an incision in the temple where the pain is located such that you can place the alum beneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is repaired, bind it tightly and hold it like this for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then untie it and treat with strong garlic juice, leaving the wound like this for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then apply cotton soaked in butter until it forms a crust.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment, cure the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see fit to use some of the caustic medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on caustic medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	It is called a "closure" because its head has the shape of a closed fist with one curve and in the middle it has a small prominence.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, hold your hand and turn it slightly to one side, so that half of the blade is scorched.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	lift your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, which is outside, and let an abundance of blood flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterward, place cotton covered in linen on the wound, and leave it there for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply moist cotton with butter, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare', cover its entire tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this fresh migraine.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous cauterizations with medicine and iron are insufficient, then you must heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and incise instead on the spot with a line half an inch long, and remove your hand once, being careful not to cut the artery or reach the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and be mindful of the jaw movement when one swallows, ensuring that it does not move or cause spasms in the patient, and guard against excessive blood loss from the artery if cut, which is a great fear especially for those who are unaware and uninitiated to such matters, like students without experience.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	And leave the work halfway done;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	But I will tell you how to staunch the blood when an artery is severed, and I will show you where it occurs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is still suffering, cauterize it on top of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you observe this, apply the cautery we mentioned in the chapter on arterial extraction, using the double-bladed cautery.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And these cauteries are better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain in the ears due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear arises from coldness and one has applied solvent medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned before but the pain persists, then heat this cautery tool called a "point", of which the shape is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After pricking all around the sick ear, or around both ears if pain is felt in both, and move slightly above the root of the ear once you have marked the point to cauterize.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make X points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Wounds that must be treated with cauterization are only those caused by flux, as we mentioned in the classification of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And do not apply cauterization to similar conditions that arise from drying out or the breaking of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of wound that originates from the flow of humors and purgings of the head and gargles, and it doesn't improve, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	One at the root of the ear, another slightly beyond the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	Place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and have them cauterized at the top of the ear slightly below the crown of the head, and another one on the temple as long as a thumb.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	Leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burnt.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	It is similar in appearance to the cutellaire we described earlier, but it is a little more delicate and the knife should be slightly larger.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, leave the wound as I have said before until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but the patient does not improve and has no fever, then make four cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two above the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and another at the place called "vessel" as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And it is treated as we have said previously.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills that purify the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After having raised the head of the patient fully, place on their occiput the mustard plaster which is described in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the method of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	If you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is treated thus, it is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if he is not, perform three cauterizations on his head down to the neck, leaving a two-finger width space between each.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	Treat it as you would the others, and if you feel it necessary, and the patient can endure it, perform one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, put two others above the two horns, and treat it until it is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterization be called 'olivare', as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head must be cleansed of hairs and other things, as we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after washing the patient's head, then cauterize them on the head and on each horn, behind it, and three times along the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, then do four cauterizations along the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And leave it until the part of the heart closest to the wound is burned, then lift your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment is complete, wait until it is fully healed, and use the cautery called "olive oil," as we previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic; and it is necessary to first temper the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, when the patient is an adult and can take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, perform a gargle and chew softening the brain often with good meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After that, split the head in half lengthwise, and perform a cautery as we have said before on each side of the skull, and also over the brain.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and suffering, perform a cautery as I have described for those with paralysis and body weakness, on their spine from neck to lower back, and use olive oil in the manner that I explained before.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform a subtle cauterization according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, excesses or corrupt humidities and thick phlegm are present, then cauterize with multiple cauteries as we have mentioned for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the excesses decline towards it and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink so that their brain is cleansed, according to what was mentioned previously in this division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After rising, lift the patient's head;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Afterwards, make a linen pad well-made, like a circle, and place it in the middle of the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And have the patient lie down with crossed legs, ensuring they are well-supported on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After presenting the linen pad, you must melt some old sheep's butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	Heat it over gentle fire so that the skin tolerates its application;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	Then empty out the circle from within the head, and leave it to cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this for the patient once every week with some other good treatment until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you wish to cauterize, do so by making multiple dots along the entire length of the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then place wet cotton on top, soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	the awe of eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the awe first comes to the eyes through the signs I mentioned in the classification, then begin and give the patient something purifying for the head, protect them from all moisture, and make them sweat in the bath multiple times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards, instruct him to lie down and apply a cautery on the head, and perform two cauterizations above each of the two temples if the descent of the fluid is towards both eyes together, or one if it is directed at one eye.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	Cover the entire cautery area with gauze over all the veins and arteries that are beneath the heart, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temples.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Be wary of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with a cloth as tightly as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will instruct you on extracting arteries and performing incisions, the caution on how to staunch them.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes a cautery or excision is made below the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	The body of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to be on the veins or by the arteries that appear outside the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and it is seen that this is of cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then apply the cautery I mentioned at the beginning to the eye area.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	A cautery on the head, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or excisions below the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if more is needed, cautiously cauterize above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From the body of tears through within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and they do not improve, then give them three nights of drinking cow's urine.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king's head, cauterize the middle of the olive-shaped cautery site.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And place two 'clavilis' cauteries above the wrists, slightly below the hairline.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	Beware of the artery so as not to cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called 'olive'.
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you wish, place two additional cauteries on the wrists as long as the eyebrows are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not leave your hand there except for as long as one-third of the paper is burnt, according to the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	On the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	There are times when the eyelashes turn inward, prick the eye, and cause irritation. For this, cauterization is performed in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	That is to say, with fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and become even, then place the patient in your care.
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After, lord, on the paper of the eyes draw a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then put moist cotton in egg white and parsley mush on the eye, then heat the following cautery which is of this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterize on the drawn figure often and again until the heart is burnt in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the sign of success in this work is that you will see the paper retract and hairs raised to the edge of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand away, and leave it thus for three days, then put moist cotton in butter until the scald is gone;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, allow the wound to heal completely.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs appear, and the skin is softened, then resume the cauterization on the same spot, just as you did initially.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	If the hairs fall out, cauterize until the skin rises to its natural level, is even, and no longer pricks the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	Medical cauterizations that burn are when you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and evenly, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and quicklime, of each one ounce, and grind them together well.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	et press it with a cloth so that it does not cool down, then spread it over the shape you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place some eyes on the paper;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness is only in one eye, you must operate on that one, but if it is in both eyes as well...
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye cotton moistened with egg white.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the patient's head be on your healthy side and place your index finger pointing at the medicine, then press the pouch and mix it every time the patient feels a sensation of heat from the medicine, for they will also feel a burning sensation.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the sensation of heat passes, lift up the cloth and see if it is also raised like a leaf would be lifted by fire or an incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, apply more medicine to the place where the medicine has been applied, until your work is even, and your eyes are focused.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place moist cotton soaked in butter until the burning heart is appeased, afterward treat the place with an ointment called "diaphenes," and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must be mindful of your work, take great care that none of the medicine gets into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterward and hairs prick in the eye, repeat the medicine on this softened spot from the paper itself, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Afterward treat it until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And you should know that the eyes of men vary in size and smallness, and according to this, be your constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And let not the correct path be denied to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit it, then you must apply cautery according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place their head on your lap.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	Hold the minister's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or twist its neck.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	Afterwards, place moistened cotton below an egg or in parsley juice over the eye.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	Afterwards, heat the cautery which is such:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaved at the head like the shape of a vaulted roof, along with where the cauterization is to be done;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one side of the head to the other, and if you see, it should also look like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nevertheless, this one who is shaved is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After that, press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, then dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, operate on it, and draw out the poison forcefully.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after that, place the hot cautery on it properly, and keep your hand on the cautery at the part of the nail above the eye, so that your hand does not falter.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery into the grease of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the bone with the cautery, it would be beneficial.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, restart the cautery again, once more if needed, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After, place wet cotton soaked in butter on top, and treat with a drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and treat it according to what comes in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a type of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand the fistula, and split the site open;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Afterwards, place into the fissure one subtle camel's hair of which it is made:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	Et they make it to the quantity of one third of a plank.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	Et hold your hand or arm firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run into his eye.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And one must put on the patient's eye moist cotton with egg white or honey.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The lead fills the place of the fistula, and the wound heals miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, you must administer a perforation with a knife, and return the fistula to the body of the knife according to what is necessary in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks occur on lips, which are called "scabs," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it into the crevices until it reaches the bottom.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards clean the area of wax so that it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from an abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the uvula, palate, or tooth roots, it causes decay and swelling, becomes inflamed, and develops into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And treat it as we have said in the previous section, but it does not heal.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Then you must apply cauterization according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the hole or opening of the fistula, hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom and passes through it.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Do this once or twice, then treat it as we have described in the treatment section until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if they are cured thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, one must expose the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in this chapter.
dou movement des dens	By the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it does not help, then place the patient's head on your thigh.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after, heat the cautery as follows: place a cane over the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the hot cautery inside it until your hand is warm enough that the patient feels heat reaching the tooth's root.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After lifting your hand, resume the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After that, fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and hold it there for an hour; rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth is confirmed to be stable, the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of pain in the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from coldness, whether it be cold or hot, and medical treatments are ineffective, then cauterization is necessary in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	Cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization with butter is such that you take cow's butter and put it in the end of an iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	After that, take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a probe, then moisten it in melted butter, and place it on the aching tooth until it cools down.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And so it often happens that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you want to wet wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and apply a hot iron until the fire reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauterization by fire is such that you take a cane of iron or copper, and make it thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which its shape will come about, place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cauterization is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be relieved that very day or the next morning.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter during the urgency of this cautery, and then let the cold (or ice) come after.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and here is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make the cautery for the jaw, as you wish, according to what power (or ability) you have;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and here is the shape of the cane:
des scrophules	Des scrophules
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is caused by cold and moist humours, and it does not respond to treatment with medicine, then heat the pointed cautery which follows after in this shape, and have two openings for the smoke to exit on the other side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and apply a hot cauterizing agent to the abscess once or twice as needed until it reaches the base of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cauterizing agent according to its size, leaving it for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and place moist cotton soaked in butter over the burn until it is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterward, treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is fully healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture accumulates in the body's channels, especially when it originates from a cold constitution, the patient must first be emptied through dissolvant medications;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	afterward, apply a cauterizing agent to the root of the throat, being careful not to reach the throat and only burning a small portion of the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After making another cauterization at the junction of the neck and spine, perform the cauterization called 'clavicle', as described previously.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the area just like we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	Whenever any lung disease is caused by cold dampness, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and it is an old illness, then perform two cauterizations on the corresponding meridians.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And another cauterization in the middle of the chest between two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	And these cauterizations should be called 'clavicle' according to the previously mentioned shape or method.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see fit, perform cautery by pricking with the entire point which is called "punctum," as described before in ear disease.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the pricking be down to XXX or around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the site according to what has been said before, let there be three rows of cautery marks in this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, you do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, remind the patient of his back and side.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after that, lift up the heart which is within the tickler with two of your left hand's fingers;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat up the cautery which has two iron handles as described before:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterise the heart until it is perforated to its side, and you will get a figure of four cauteries.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason cautery is performed with the three-iron cautery, hence the form of cauterization has six cauteries.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerve follows the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the three-iron cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted to this one nerve, so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Then apply the cautery, pound bell peppers with salt;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well-settled.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again soon after, then this indicates that there are underlying problems; thus perform a cautery on the thick part above the clavicle, or many cauterizations when needed.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture has been removed, and the patient healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach coldness and too much moisture come such that it is extracted from its complexion, and the catarrh multiplies for him despite usual treatments providing no benefit, then the patient should be reminded to lie on their back with legs and arms stretched out.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	In this procedure, make three cauterizations underneath the armpit with as much space as two fingers, to each clavicle cautery, and two cauterizations outside on both sides so that the shape of the cauterization is a triangle, and leave such distance between them that they do not join together when the flesh rots.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterization be so thorough that it purifies both parts of the heart; and let the shape of the cauterizations follow this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form:
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and for him who fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach there. Puncturing according to the quantity you desire to insert;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with all the 'point' cautery.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we had previously, let it heal.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver experiences pain from cold and moisture and due to excessive wind, such that it is removed from its natural state by superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said previously about divisions, but it does not benefit them, so the patient must be reminded of their illness and its severity.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and for a third-degree cautery, the signs are as follows: this form and this image with these quantities on the liver, under the hypochondrium where the man's ribs come together.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and leave space between each cautery equal to the width of your thumb.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the length of each cautery match that of the body part being treated, not pressing too hard with your whole hand throughout the entire procedure.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and burn only half of the heart-shaped cautery, keeping the patient upright on their feet throughout the procedure.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	and if your intention is to cauterize these cautery wounds with the surgical knife, provided that you are skilled and wise in this art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, as you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and do not let it reach the mouth, for the heart is very delicate in that area, and you would dry it out to see it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is within the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too severe.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the membrane, they feel excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And so when this treatment is required, the patient must be reminded of it on their head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	Then cut away the flesh where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray; this is its form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	Cauterize with the cautery until the heart is burnt, and go as far as the saphenous vein, so that all flesh is destroyed.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment according to the type of cloth used until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And it is not appropriate for anyone but those who have studied medicine extensively to use this cautery treatment, by whose hands these ailments were cured at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can operate boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of hard wax
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make many cauteries with the roots of aristolochia, and in this way:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take one long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and also as thick and as long as your two fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	Oil the root and place it in the fire, then cauterize with one cautery between the forearm and neck, and two small cauteries a little lower down on the part that is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And two cauteries between the fifth rib and sixth, inclining slightly backwards;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery between the breasts, and another on the stomach, and two between the shoulders, and two on either side of the breast outside the cautery that is between the shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not squeeze your hand, but apply pressure gently as if scenting.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancient sources say that no man should use fire cautery like a barber's tool, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs until it reaches this abscess;
