Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Things by which wounds are made are through striking with a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or from a lance, stick, arrow, or similar objects.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or they are made according to the locations of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, head, foot, stomach, liver, and similar parts.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And we shall tell you the treatment for each wound, beginning with simple head wounds since memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and the bone is not broken, take heed if it's from striking with a stone or similar objects, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you slightly suspect of an impending abscess.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If you must do so, then bleed from the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and make sure to bleed on the opposite side of the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And let the patient rid themselves of fullness from wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if they do not wish to be bled, let their meat intake be reduced, and they should neither drink wine nor eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place on the wound cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine, if hot abscesses form there.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound powder which I shall name shortly, should it be fresh with all its blood and not moved by air.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with sutures, then bring them together with stitching, as I will explain for wounds of the abdomen, regarding the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone, deep, and holds only by a little bit of skin, cut it off.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then treat the wound with medication and restore hard flesh in place of leather, instruct the patient to eat coarse meats like beef and pork, as well as chicken and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find the leather is corrupted but it does not reach to the bone, cut out all of the corruption and throw it away, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein that does not stop bleeding and cannot be stopped with medicine, tie off the artery and if you find it has slipped, bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not benefit him, then cauterize him.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, so is the treatment light.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And you must put this powder on it as soon as the rust has been removed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way of making the powder is as follows:
pren encens une partie;	Take one part incense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood, two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Galangal root, three parts, and finely powder it, then apply to the wound, pressing firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, leaving it unbound, if it does not swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one must remove the medicine only when it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only the alum is used when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the cold has moved from the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has killed the wound, especially deep ones, do not put any of this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some soothing ointments, or a poultice of barley flour made with water and honey, until it flows freely.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with delicate pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you about fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	Of the neck wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no significant difference between this and a head wound; however, if the windpipe or artery in the neck is severed...
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nose, there is no other remedy except to leave it alone and not put anything constricting on it, for this harms the nose and makes it retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the nature of the nose is cold, and its proximity extends to the brain, which is the most vital organ.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medicine be soothing, as warm water washed in soft oil, and mixed with cucumber also washed in sweet water, and other stones of salt according to this method, and moist salves.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind with bandages, then let it heal until it is completely closed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and have fur and pus in them, pierce it or make an incision below this point.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then open it up, and suture it, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spinal cord in the throat is cut, or the heart and vessels are damaged, take care that flesh does not go into it. Cut the heart's conduit upon the neck of the throat, but do not damage the throat itself when you reset it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	then hold it carefully in place for a few days, then treat it with draining ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has penetrated to the bone, examine it closely.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are fragments of bone in it, then remove them forcefully where you can, and for those you cannot retrieve, leave them to fester until the wound suppurates. Alleviate the pain and ease the discharge from the sore.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed a fistula, treat it as I have explained in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of wounds from lances or knives.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, examine whether air escapes from the wound when the patient walks around.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood intact, do not apply the powder immediately nor bind it to prevent the blood from flowing out freely, as it returns to the heart, and this can kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton into the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days or four days or longer.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	there will not be any spasm, nor evil heart tremors or shortness of breath
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good condition of the bones, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it with tents and other remedies until it is completely cured.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and there is some work done on it again, then you should know that there is a fistula there.
si la cure si com on doit.	then treat it as one ought to.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, whether it be on the chest or back, treat what is in front first.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, stitch it.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if it is small, use powder. If the wound is deep and has pierced the bone, splitting into pieces, clean the wound thoroughly, and realign the broken bones if they are displaced.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if the bones are not displaced, leave the wound to fester so that it drains itself.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on different body parts, the treatment is as we have stated before.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Abdominal hernia.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	Ruptures of the abdomen are large, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Of a large wound sometimes the intestines or their nerves will protrude, which allows for air entry.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because you must be extra careful to push the intestines back in without tearing them.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Because the intestines swell and become sensitive to cold, they are harder to push back in without damaging them further; thus, it is better to treat the smaller wound first so that you can carefully guide the intestine back into place before treating the other injuries.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	Know that there are four types of abdominal ruptures:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common ruptures occur in the abdominal wall suture, and the sutures of other wounds on the body are the same as for other injuries.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more suitable with the stitching of the abdomen; I will speak about each one individually and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine comes out, and it is necessary to put it back in, this can be done through one of two methods.
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either due to the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or soft cloth in warm water only, which you have boiled in hot water with vinegar and spice, and apply it to the intestine until the swelling is reduced.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And sometimes this constraining wine is made sour to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with water or other infusions and let the mallows be cooked because this alleviates the entry of too much.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if nothing enters it, then make an opening in the wound with an instrument used to cut hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to ensure that we do not cut unless there is great need for it.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments used to make an incision:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	when it cuts inside in an arc shape and not outwards, observe here its form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have fallen out, you must replace them back inside according to their natural form in its proper place, if you are able, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is located below the belly, you must lay the patient on their back, with their legs elevated above their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	And if the wound is below the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; likewise, if the rupture in the abdomen occurs in one of its two halves, position them so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	Thus, it is necessary to manage as I say for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, use the equipment provided to you, then take it in your hands and apply a gentle substance that covers the entire rupture with your palm, bringing together its lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two sides of the leather with the two sides of the syphon, which is beneath the leather inside, so that you make it pierced from this part, and gather the two heads of the siphon together in four parts.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then draw out a double thread around the needle in two parts, then gather together the two sides of the wound appropriately, and then leave two fingers' width, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread with a knot as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to continue in this way according to your need of needles until the entire wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and thick, for fine needles cut all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For this reason they must be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not suitable to push the needles too far beyond the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and open the wound before it heals;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when they move, and place tents or small cloths over the needle heads to keep them in place, leaving them there until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this manner of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second type of suture is common, and it involves bringing together the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue with an needle or thick moderate thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these four heads together, return the needle to the part where you started, in the manner one sews cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave some space between each suture as thick as two fingers.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	these sutures are useful for the man; I sewed a wound on someone's stomach, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was larger than a palm, with the intestines protruding two palms in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days; I treated him and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, but this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And apply old cotton on top of the wound twice a day, and wash it with water and honey until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	One shall say two proper ways of stitching/suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and insert it from outside to inside part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	Once it has pierced through the skin from right to right, leave the head of the siphon or incision where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce on the other side from inside to outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this suture is that you should sew it just like furriers make furs, leaving one side of the siphon untied and taking it up on the other, until the whole suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, as Galen accurately describes it, is done in this way: One joins the two parts together naturally and aligns one end of the wound with the other, like so...
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle at the wound's edge nearest to the navel, piercing just that spot, and leave both ends of the wound untouched.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle around and pierce through from outside to inside, passing it between both ends of the wound.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Next, pierce both ends from outside to inside in two other places of the wound that are on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is Galen's second method for suturing, which is also the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galiens said these words, and some bear witness, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in a manner like those who sew leather straps;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and understand that when the rupture is within the belly, the suture is more grievous than other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, rather than moved by the burning [coals], then return the intestine and the cut.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put on top of it some powder made from burnt animal fat, and if the burn has moved away from the ointment, then apply a different ointment that is ready to hand until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And tie it up with thread, and seal it with hot wax.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound like any other until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicine, then apply old cotton wool as soon as it begins to heal, and move it around twice a day until the wound is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you will need no other medicine in many treatments where the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound will poison vital body parts, then it is necessary to soak a light linen cloth in tepid oil or rosehip oil and place it around the affected area and under the armpit.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or swelling in his bowels, which often happens, then administer a clyster of tepid black wine, especially if the inflammation has reached the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called "jeun," cannot heal when injured due to the layout of their veins and the delicate nature of the entire body, as well as its proximity to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	and if the belly bursts from the wound, put it back in place just like with the intestine while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned worms or black, you must bind the place that has turned black so no blood flows from there, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the binding and hang both heads from the lower part of the wound until outside to ease extraction when the belly falls, and the wound opens.
de la routure dou boueil	From a broken jaw.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are round and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I saw a man pierced in the belly by a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which issued waste matter and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to my ability, and I did not cease from cauterizing until he was healed, and the flesh had fused together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it fused, I suspected that the patient might have pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no discomfort there, but remained in good health, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experts say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take large pieces of meat, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the meat has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it tightens its mouth on top.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then cut the head of the meat and keep it so that it cannot be untied, then place another piece of meat afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	These meats heal in the intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, and if one wants to sew the intestine with a fine thread which can be cut from the intestine of an animal, it should be done this way.
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this thread of intestine, which should be very clean, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine linen thread twisted together, then insert the thread into the needle, and pass it through the intestine, and draw it back up through the rupture.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this manner of sewing together is not false but according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the delicate intestines, there is no remedy nor cure but skill and expertise.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is complete and turns inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is truly an erroneous hard white knotting, where there is no pain felt, and it also looks like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear bowels, and other times dense.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed and lacks flesh, this is only due to one of nine reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, due to the scarcity of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or due to the hard flesh within it, and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much bowel;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Where the flesh is swollen, and the substance is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not effective in treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where due to this, the corruption is like a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where due to the properties of the region, digestion is slow, health restoration is delayed, and it is swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are wounds or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, the signs, and the treatments with medicine in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now you must let me inform you of the treatment for a fistula, which is performed by manual operation.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistulas occur in any part of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the hip, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it reaches such that comes to the main member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only hard work and ignorance involved;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have faith in its treatment, and you know how to identify it, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, insert it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, search for it with a subtle thread of flax, because the flaxen thread bends to follow the twists and turns.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot locate it precisely with threads, then cleanse and irrigate it through one of the apertures, for moisture travels from one aperture to another, cleaning and purging.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then examine it carefully to the best of your ability, determine if there are any bones or nerves present, and check if it is completely healed over, ask the patient about any pain they feel when you apply pressure with your hand, as well as its location.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and once you have accurately located its position, whether it is near a joint, nerve, artery or vein, or in any of the areas I mentioned earlier, treat it according to what I said, and remove any pus or corrupted flesh that may be inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is indeed deep in the right spot, you must remove it perfectly as much as possible. Then insert moist bandages soaked in healing medicines and push them inside the fistula so that the medicine corrodes any remaining superfluous matter at its base
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply healing ointments that promote healthy flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it does not heal with this treatment, cauterize as we have explained earlier; and should the bone be affected by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	Should neither vein nor nerve constrict your principal limb as we have said earlier;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, leave it until all corruption is removed, then treat secondary infections with ointments until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healed, and sinks back as before, know that you have not reached the bottom of it.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If you uncover it and dig until you reach the depth, remove all corruption, then replace it in its place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is another tool left by nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone inside, and you can extract it with forceps, remove it using an appropriate instrument for this purpose; and if there are many bones, extract all of them, do not leave even one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture causes resistance, and there is no error or fear, cut through the moisture, flesh, and bone, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something that encourages putrefaction to the wound, and leave it until the flesh is rotten all around the bones, then they will be easier to extract.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, like from the leg or thigh, wash away the putrefaction until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if a large part is corrupted, and it reaches down to the bone marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	you must saw it and cut it all away until you reach the corrupted part, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to an internal issue, causing matter to gather and form an abscess, which swelled greatly but had no external cause for incision.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the surgeons, in their foolishness, worked on it so much that they opened the abscess and removed a great deal of matter, which turned into a fistula, and many holes formed, all expelling foul-smelling moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many doctors tried to cure him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the treatments he was undergoing, and what was passing through the large abscesses.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body would turn red, with a yellowish complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that each came toward the other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hurried and cut into one of the abscesses until I exposed part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with decay reaching deep inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be the corrupted bone, hoping there was no further decay beyond what I extracted.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with moistened medicines over a long time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found that the decay had spread into the bone and its marrow, and then I removed it, and tried to close the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do so before cutting around one palm's width of the bone, and its marrow was completely decayed, then I restored it with medicine.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the patient's weakness, who could not bear it, and my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation, he often bled excessively, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, hard tissue grew, which was well-formed, caused no harm whatsoever, and did not hinder him at all, either going or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, one must treat it in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take the ligament, and pull it to the head of the protruding bone, and instruct someone to lift it upwards.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	Attach another piece of linen thread that is thicker than the first ligament, and bind it over the flesh above the bone, stretch out the head, such that you draw the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh on the spot where you wish to operate, so that the knife does not cut into the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	Place hot iron or a board beneath the bone to press against the corrupted flesh in order to cut it away.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	One must treat as much as one is able to see and feel the corruption, and then treat again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then place the hot iron underneath, and then cover it from one part to the other over the corruption, and let the poultice be as long as the length of the corruption with the iron, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and cover the bone on one side to the other.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the space between two joints, there is nothing else to cut out but this.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, it is very difficult, but nevertheless you must inquire about this corrosion and how it opens for you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in every way you can, but let neither vein nor nerve oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	know that there are many cutting instruments and threads to cut these bones, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and delicacy, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this it is necessary to adapt each similar piece of work with its tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to your understanding of this art and the signs of different illnesses.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	therefore choose the tool you need according to what is required.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints can dislocate either internally or externally;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated that inflammation with medicine through the treatment of wounds, and it does not improve, then you must cut off that limb up to the place where the corrosion begins so that the patient escapes death or the evil, which is greater, of losing a limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the sign is that the limb turns black as if it has been burned by fire, and afterward it may turn purple, for this corrosion of a limb can spread from member to member and take over the whole body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	So do not delay in cutting it off, and if the corrosion is caused by the poison of certain venomous creatures such as the scorpion fish, snake, or similar, and it has started at the top of the arm, cut it there and do not give any space for it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, treat the joint so that the decay does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, treat it with a knife;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there are no strong remedies except for those that match its power;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same when decay appears in the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it reaches the first joint, treat it after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it appears in the foot, treat the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises to the leg, treat at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it [the dislocation] comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the way to cut or sever the limb is that you bind it above and below, and have some ministers hold one binding down, and other ministers hold the other binding up, and you separate the flesh between the two bindings with a wide-bladed chisel, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then cut or sever it, and place a linen cloth on either side so that the wound does not touch healthy flesh, and prevent further injury and hot abscesses from forming in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if there is bleeding when you operate, cauterize the place immediately, or apply some clotting powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I shall tell you what happened to a man in his sleep:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a dark patch that resembled a burn from fire, and this corrosion started first in his big toe, spreading until it covered the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	When the man saw the corrosion, he immediately decided to amputate his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	Long after, the corrosion returned to his finger on his hand, and he came to me. I applied resonant substances to it after cleansing his body, but the corruptions could not be stopped.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he saw that I cut off his hand, and I would not, for I had hope of curing the disease;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, for the strength of man was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he became desperate, returned to his land, took up an axe to cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have not concealed it from you except so that one might do otherwise if need be.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in the flesh and remains so long that it causes a great accumulation of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it swells up and bursts open, ejecting the pus which leaves the place bare like a hollow vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is as delicate as thin fabric, and it does not extend to the bone or the nerve; such an illness is called a "shin," and it is not called a "fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you must cut around this skin, especially when it is delicate, like a thin piece of fabric;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not fear its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are concerned that the skin will rot, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it thus with a clyster:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the breast is large, and the bowels emit a foul odour, then administer an Egyptian medicated enema made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take alum, oil, and litharge in equal parts, put them to cook in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	Then take the amount you need of this medicine, mix it with water and honey, and administer an enema to the breast, holding the orifice closed.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by smelling.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Repeat this procedure as many times as necessary until the breast is healed and the pus removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes it is cleansed with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and you take the ash from wood of vine, pour water over it, then let it drip through, and cleanse with it, as long as you know that the breast is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes, then cleanse them with water and honey where they have a little powdered litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you cleanse them with honey and mixed wine, as the honey has properties to clean and wash, and the wine makes the blood rise.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well cleansed, then cleanse it with something that makes flesh grow in it, and it is that you take definitive ointment, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Where you can apply some medicine and ointments to it, of which I have already spoken about their properties in the chapter on ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the hole in the breast is small and the nozzle of the clyster cannot enter, then you should widen it a little with an iron instrument, and insert either a piece of Egyptian cloth or Basilicum ointment until it has been enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, you should cut it and leave only a place where the clyster can enter; and if the hole that leaks is above, then cover it with something or put something in a lower position than it.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is intact, nothing should be allowed to enter it.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cut the vein as you wish, devise a way for the bowels to descend to their lowest point, because when the bowels are full, they prevent the entry of food; and if you cannot cut the vein as you wish, then devise it in such a manner...
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowels gently move downwards, and do not leave any of the bowels there.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to place on the wound, and stretch them over a linen cloth that covers the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut as deeply as necessary at the spot of the vein, making a hole wider than the first one, then spread soft ointment on another piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and place it over the wound to alleviate the bowels, and do not remove the large outer bandage for several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is on the breast wound often removes it to remove the bowels, and examines that which flows from the bowels, whether it be poison or pus or something else, or if it is digestible or not.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way that you see nature rising above the breast wound, then know that the breast already scars, and approach the recovery.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then release it in the morning or on the third day, and when you free the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the subtle poison slowly diminishes over a long time, do not despair of recovery, for healing is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if an indigest substance comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast heals slowly and is remote, apply drying medicines which are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as definite ointment, for it contains a great part of vitriol, and this is the final medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take definite ointment, and make it with rose oil, and mix in equal parts of old wine.
puis le confit et en use;	then melt it and apply it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same treatment works better when thickened and cooked, if definite ointment is not available, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind it, and sprinkle the powder over honey while it's still on the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	Then glue I a pad, and extend it over the breast, and sometimes administer a long astragalus root, and roots of celestial lily, which is like flour made from vetch and centaury.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and I use simple or compound medicines
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make powder out of it, and put on the honey I mentioned before, then apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is elongated and does not heal with this treatment, know that the corruption has reached perfection, and it has penetrated into the bone or hard tissues.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	treat the wound as if it were a fistula, like we mentioned before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises underneath the fingernail of the hand, or the toenail, and sometimes appears in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it becomes inflamed and is not treated promptly, an abscess develops, spreading pus that erodes the nail bed until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes even removing the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	It causes bone corrosion, leading to painful decay, the joint of the finger becomes wide and loose, and the flesh turns a bad colour.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment is not beneficial, then you must cut away all that remains of the nail with an iron tool, then cauterise the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is very effective treatment when the bone is healthy and the nail undamaged.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	But if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick it, piercing and wounding it, you should place a probe underneath the nail at the point where it pierces the flesh, lift up the injured area of flesh gently, and remove any remaining tissue with sharp, corrosive medicines.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, remove it, and treat with force, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the finger corrupted, cut it off just below the first knuckle as described earlier, then treat until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is pierced, and swells up, causing great pain, you must treat the wound first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail with a sharp spoon-shaped tool, cutting across it, and be careful not to reach the flesh beneath the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on it to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the wrist joint from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some men have very fleshy index fingers that may contain bone and sometimes even a nail; they can be born with growths at the root of their knuckles or anywhere on their fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born on the right side of their head never move [their eyes], but those who are born at the junction of the eye may move it;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The stature of one who is fleshy is slight, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Operate on him at the base of his spine with a wide spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	One who is born at the root of the jaw is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	So you must operate with care.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those born on the inside of the fingertip, you must first cut away the surrounding flesh down to the bone and then amputate the bone with a fine saw; treat the wound until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The injuries that cause two bones to come together can occur through birth, or by sudden wounding, burning from fire, or similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You should then operate on that suture so that the teeth are replaced according to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or moistened cloth with rose oil, so they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or place between two soft planks until the colors are fused, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a person has sutures in their palm, cut this suture as appropriate.
des vils	Of the wrist.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large open vessels filled with melancholy humours that arise in various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And they occur more frequently in the legs of those who walk on foot and work, carrying loads, more so than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	You must therefore administer purging of bile to them at times, and then treat with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron treatment is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is where they cauterize, draining the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other method is that you lift the vein and draw all of its contents out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting [or surgery] goes as follows:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Raise the first leg with very hot water until the large veins become thin and subtle. Then stretch out the patient's leg from above the thigh down to just below the knee joint.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in an I-shape, or II-shape, or III-shape with a wide incision. Draw out and squeeze the dark blood into your hand, from one end to another until such time that sufficient blood has been evacuated according to the patient's needs.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it [the wound], and instruct the patient to abstain from meat for a while, eating black pudding instead.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And repeat the evacuation [of blood] and cauterization when the veins become full again, causing harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The healing of wounds follows this method:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Trim the hair from the patient's leg if it is hairy, then place them in a bath, and bathe their leg with warm water until the skin turns red, and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have access to a bath, heat it over the fire, and then rub directly onto the vein from below the knee down to the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then work the skin with an unciner, and peel back the vein from either side until it is exposed where you can feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And when the vein appears red and black, and as it enters the flesh, it looks like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then push the vein underneath until it is raised above the skin, and then draw it to the small knife, then cut it in another place further up by three fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the small knife like you have done before, and draw it to another small knife, just as you did initially.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then make another cut, or more if you need them, then lift the skin and cut it with the toe of your foot, then draw and lift it until you reach the second small knife.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it from cut to cut until it is completely outside, then make the final cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot draw and lift it out, then insert a needle with a strong doubled thread through it, tie the ends together, insert it under the vein, turn your hand one way and other until it comes away.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure it does not break, for if it breaks, one cannot pull or lift it, which is harmful to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it entirely, place on the wound site damp wool soaked in wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the bone is contracted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it unevenly, but do not break it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it as we mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one breaks the bone is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not damage the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is a large curved blade because if it were slender, it would rupture the vein but being thick as we have said and here is its form:
de la voinne civile	From the civilized vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is situated in the legs, in warm parts where no grass or tree grows and on land that has no moisture.
