et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and at times it appears in other parts apart from the legs and this happens due to gangrene that develops under the skin just as serpents and worms develop inside the body, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a great inflammation comes into the leg, then its color changes, and the vein starts to protrude outwardly, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound opens, you must wrap around it a piece of cloth that is 3.5 to 7 inches long, tie it and leave the cloth hanging from the leg, and every time it comes off, rewrap it with the cloth and retie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap the remaining hair around, and do not cut it at its root, so that it grows back completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will enter the flesh, causing abscesses and rot in that place, resulting in a severe illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	so that is why it must be treated quickly and completely, leaving nothing on the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this wound can be as long as five palms or more, and a man came to me with a wound that was ten palms in length. When you cut it open, push one finger into the opening, and pierce it all the way through so everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And empty the matter that is inside, and bring healing medicines to prevent rot one day, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this wound is minor, especially when it appears at the ankle or foot joints where there is a lot of perforation and must be kept dry.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "ox disease" in our land because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body up and down, and one can feel its movement from limb to limb until it tears the skin where it was and falls out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and they are caused by a corruption of certain humours, just as maggots, worms, and intestinal parasites come into being in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is doubt about its nature, for when it moves through the body and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and drained, there is no way to prevent its spread except when it moves.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it is necessary then that you bind the place above and below with a strong and tight bandage, then cut over it and drain it forcefully, and if the maggot has penetrated perfectly into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it causes is when it runs into the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, firmly restrain your eyebrow underneath, then push up and pull it away.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and the patient should use cleansing body treatments with dissolving medicinal solutions to remove bad humours and rotten flesh.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From pain due to windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, it's a pain that comes to certain limbs and can move from limb to limb.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see an ill woman, who uncovered her arm for me revealing a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and then soon after, you see it rise up like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, just like quicksilver when it falls from above.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from that place and lodges in the shoulder, then a little while later spreads throughout the body until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it would circle back around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed by how it moved from limb to limb because I had never seen this illness behave in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had heard often that pain could move from one place to another, but I never believed it until I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought that it was because the woman had a thin body and her veins were exposed, and so this wind-like force appeared to be constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not follow this reasoning for those who are delicate, with moist bodies and open wounds.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	When you treat this illness and the patient experiences such pain, if it presents as we have described, bind it above and below firmly, then cut into it until that windiness is forced back to its place.
et cauterize le leu;	And cauterise the area.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If you do not see it with your own eyes, treat it for what causes windiness, as bitter pills, and pills of serpent's flesh, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their variations are such that some have large spikes, others small, some hairy, others smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And for those with two edges, and those with tongues, and for those which have parts.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls on any member does so in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or it falls on principal members such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then on any place within these organs, and the sign of death that I will tell you about follows:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must take care with the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of a brain injury when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and lifts the covering membrane above the brain, is when there are scotomata (blind spots) and sudden pain in the eyes, and swelling and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and impaired reasoning, and vomiting bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without breath from the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps he loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and white moisture oozes from the wound resembling pulsation, and there also comes out something like burnt flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then attend to the cure, and extract the arrow if it is there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow when it hits the heart are: that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if lodged in a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves with each pulse, and black blood flows out, bringing coldness and cold sweat, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	you must then surely know that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that an arrowhead has not penetrated is if there is no foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's colour changes, and they breathe heavily and seek cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow hits near the shoulder blade, it is close to the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	it causes great pain and suffering and heavy sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs of the shoulders become numb.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls on the stomach, perhaps something undigested may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly and no excrement comes out of the lower intestine, there is little hope for a cure or extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps and flows out, and the patient feels intense pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, like the face, neck, throat, shoulder, arm, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and legs, as well as similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man, an arrow fell onto his arm at the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and drew it out from beneath the ear's fatty tissue, and he was healed without complication.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in another case, I extracted an arrow that had lodged in the eye's fatty tissue beneath the conjunctiva; the arrowhead was missing, and only its tip could be felt towards the shaft. The arrow was large, made entirely of light iron without barbs.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was healed, and no misfortune befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And draw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barbs, and worked carefully until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw an arrow from the man, which was lodged in his thigh or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days, there was no change in his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, engineered it, and drew it out, and he had no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow having fallen to his back or side, and the wound is closed over.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and if the arrow remains inside him, and it does not alter his natural functions, nor does it cause any harm to any of his natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man, with an arrow having fallen to his face, and the wound is closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remains there without causing him great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And draw an arrow from the king's face, which was stuck in his nose and was slightly leaning to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	And the arrow was completely buried.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for treatment after it had been cut three days ago.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed it with great care, but did not feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt pain and pressure beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow, so I applied an attractive and digestive poultice there to prevent the flesh from swelling.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the flesh around the arrow appeared swollen.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I left the poultice there for two days, and this resolved the wound initially, but then the patient suffered long-term effects until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	And he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound by hand during daytime, while it was open, and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow move towards its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I adjusted the arrow's position in the wound using that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And it took around four months for the tissues to heal completely. Then I widened the wound and inserted pliers into it, and moved them from side to side, but the arrow could not be extracted.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	So I did not stop experimenting and devising different instrument techniques until one day I took the pliers, which were well-made according to what is described at the end of this chapter, and with them, I gripped the arrow and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you focus your attention on what I do not say, because a book cannot cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But wise masters build upon very little, and on what is presented to them they find new methods and new tools for the treatment of strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not leave the members in which they are stuck for two reasons:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Where by low place where they enter, or from another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which jumps from where it enters, is an arrow embedded in the flesh, and sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh is rotten around it, and ease its exit.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it is embedded in the bone, and cannot be removed, leave it thus for a few days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it will jump out, and if it does not, pierce around with a fine awl until the flesh around is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head, reaching one of the brains ventricles, and some of the accidents I have mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	you must not remove it but leave it there until the wound around it becomes even after several days because if the arrow reaches the brain surface, death will follow.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in the bone, and does not come out through the skin, and the patient remains well for a few days without any bad incidents, then devise a way to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if the arrow is deeply embedded in this way that it cannot be extracted easily, administer cauterization around it as I have instructed you previously.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep within the body so that it cannot be seen but we feel its presence then seek it all over.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, draw it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot remove it due to the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrowhead, and there is no bone, nerve or vein involved, then make an incision so that the wound becomes larger;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place, remove the flesh that is attached to it on both sides as much as possible, then break or bend the ears of the arrowhead until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Do this carefully so that you do not break the arrowhead, as it would be more difficult to remove if broken.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding tissue is rotten, then pull it out, for its extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the loss of blood troubles you, perform as we have said regarding treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	watch out for the incision of the nerve and the vein, and use a device as you can extract the arrow without danger, either soon or later, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	place the patient according to how they were positioned when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help available, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow that comes from another place, or where nothing appears to come out of it, or the skin is swollen in that area if you can see or feel it obviously:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut above then, until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	If you jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained within the bone, rotate your hand circularly until you enter into the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it there for now, then resume extraction until it has emerged;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is in there, push against the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is broken off, and you wish to administer pushing, use a tapered instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the hollow of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	then push it in, and if the arrow is tapered, insert the instrument point first to aid extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all of the flesh around it if possible, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls on the foot or thigh or stomach or bladder or side, and it is close by, and you can cut above it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	Be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then extract it, and finally suture the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat [the wound] until it is clean.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is its form [shape]:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways to do this.
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, depending on the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the driving instrument is also like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as here [the figure] shows its form.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pincers to use for insertion and extraction is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins which we heal from, sixteen of them are in the head, to wit:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins that are located behind the ears, which are called "herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are visible in the temples.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are located in the corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead.
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the nose.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two goitres that are on the neck.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are located above the upper lip of the mouth, which are called "augeherich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins which are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly treated are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which comes from the left side of the chest, and people call it "the head vein.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the median is called "fast," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, which people call the "heart vein.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and people call it the "belly vein," and it lies above the muscle, and it is the one that is treated, as it appears clearly on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	The salve is the vein located between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	In the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is located on the underside of the arch of the left foot, and the second one is at the ankle joint on the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein that is called "nerve", which is located at the ankle on the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg there are three veins underneath these ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins located behind the ears helps with chronic colds and headaches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you lift the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then hold the patient's neck with a cloth, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	feel them with your fingers, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, make an incision there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet and push it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the whole length of the vein, cutting through both skin and vein with two fingers, and let out blood until you see fit;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Strain it and tie it tightly until it is clean.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken about the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	Bleeding the two arteries located in the temples is beneficial for treating chronic and severe migraine, persistent ophthalmia, and excessive tearing from the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	The qualities of a good bleeder are as I have described:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	When the patient grasps their neck tightly, you will notice that both veins are clearly visible.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And if you feel numbness below your finger, proceed with bleeding above it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Raise the heart up to the vein above your index finger, insert the lancet below it, lift the vein upwards and scrape it, just as you did with the other two veins, then let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and place your finger on the wound for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then form a bandage over it, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have previously discussed the cauterization process, as well as bloodletting and its extraction, which was mentioned at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting from the vein on the forehead is just as effective as bleeding from the temporal artery for ailments of the face, such as old age symptoms, headaches, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	Its quality is such that the patient twists their neck rigidly until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "the fossor," whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point over the vein, press it with your hand or something else, and let blood flow out according to the quantity you desire.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's collarbone, and bind the wound so that it is tight but not too constricted, leaving some room for air to pass through occasionally.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the bandage should not be too tight or sharp-edged.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Bind it diagonally, for the bone is close to the surface, and by chance the bandage may break if it is too thin or delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The draining of the two veins located in the temples aids the eyes, and treats inflammation, redness, itching within the eye, and conditions affecting the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is such that patients must strain their necks by twisting with a cord, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then treat the wound, and let the healing go through transversely, a little of the long side of the flame and a bit wider, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, they may break by chance;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, binding it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The healing of the vein in the nose is good for fever, and sudden headaches, and illnesses of the face, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the vein is such that the patient tightens their neck, then pull your nose to your left hand, and take the fine long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily there, and blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	do not go too deep, and allow the blood to flow according to your need, then bandage it for a night, as it heals rather quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The vein of the two temples aids in narrowing the forehead, and at the beginning of mascle-making, and for many diseases, impetigo, corrosion, herpes, and erysipelas;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the nature of the bleeding is such that the patient should strangle their neck between two points, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the master stand above the patient's head, and the patient should sit on a seat. Then open the vein of the arm widely for a short length, then draw blood temperately as much as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then repeat the same process on the other arm, then untie the ligature, and hold all veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave him until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bloodletting of the lips,
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The draining of veins above the lips aids in healing mouth sores, gum disease, cracked lips, and their surroundings.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the nature of bloodletting is to have the patient sit in front of you, holding their neck as I've said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by having small black veins surrounding them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Treat both of them, and if you do not recognize them, or are in doubt, treat the larger one on each side; also treat all of the two veins that are above and below, as it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding below the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are below the tongue aids after the bleeding of the carotid artery, and it is done at the narrowing of the throat, for diseases of the eye, and ailments of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the bleeder should be that the patient sits between your hands towards the sun, and they lift their tongue, and look beneath on each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Heal both of them then, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that we commonly heal are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by piercing with a very hot iron, or with an olive-oil based stylet so sharp it cuts like a knife, and this is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of St Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is so broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open the narrow veins that are full of clotted blood, and contain thick and cloudy blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-oil stylet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed, slender, and for bleeding delicate veins or when there is delicate yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in treating illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, chest, and belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the healer to bleed carefully, taking care of the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, it must be stopped, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be compressed but cut like a sinew.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, you must draw it out and change to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Or if you want any vein from it, or you bleed in its place the vein between the arms.
elle apert manifestement;	She clearly shows;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cap on the wound heals slowly, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the wound, you must first extend the arm and feel the area until you find the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the spot with a sign, bind the arm, and treat the slow-healing wound.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	Be careful not to cut the artery when you see the spot swollen, for that is indeed an artery.
eschui la donques.	Avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise up like a child's urine, and the blood is bright red and thin, know that it is arterial blood.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your finger on it for a while, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	If his arm is immobilized, let it be so, and do not move the patient's arm.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him be afraid, and do not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it overpowers you, and medical help is not present, then sever the artery if it is exposed, for this will stop the flow.
et estainche li sans.	And stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of fig bark, split it, and take one half, tying it securely until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the bleeding stops, that's good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop the bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stoppage of bleeding is not always helpful in many situations due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligaments.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps as it draws blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	The surgeon must be careful not to cut too deeply below, as they may hit the nerve and cause it to swell, making treatment difficult, if not impossible.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve appears often, and if it does not appear in some men due to its delicacy, you must treat it with a thin instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	remove the nerve from your power (reach).
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a wound between the two nerves, make it longer with a cut.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment of the cephalic nerve provides relief, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to treat by making an incision with the olive-shaped blade or the myrtle-shaped blade, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one should seek the lightest spot, and if one errs the first time, do not be distressed, just begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And perhaps some men's joints swell when dislocated for the first time, but it causes no serious harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is only undertaken to preserve health and avoid future illness.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins, which are located on the arm.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	These are known as the cephalic, superficial, and basilic veins.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	You must bloodlet at the beginning of spring and autumn before eating when signs of fullness are apparent.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	It is recommended to bloodlet either on the first or third day after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no determined time, but when needed, it can be done at any hour or night, during all hours and at any time.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not appropriate to bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child except for the fourth month up until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to bleed the elderly who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in any case, they should first cleanse their intestines with a light enema if there is an excess of retained feces so that the veins do not draw harmful and excessive waste from the intestines into the main organs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One should not be bled if they are overly full of meat, drunk, until the effect passes, or suffering from dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one worsens after colic pain, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent intercourse with women, laboring, staying awake, fasting, and any other cause that exhausts all strength or power whether due to weaponry or the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purify the humours gently if the blood is thick through diet and beverages and with medicine if you have that power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath if nothing opposes it to purify the blood and heal yourself from the wound in the navel area as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day against labor, fasting, lustful acts, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and lie down and be joyful, have the one being healed raised higher than you, and rub their arm two or three times then tighten the bandage moderately because if it is too tight or slack blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the incisions with a bit of old oil, then place your left index finger on that vein below the area where you want to incision, so the vein doesn't escape and miss when cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that escape like ropes when cut, and others that are full of windiness, such that when the flame is applied, it retracts from the flame, and one cannot open the vein, and so it is with these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if one opens the vein, it may be too narrow a wound, therefore cauterizers must be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the wound bleeds for the first time, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, try again slightly below that place or above it, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient becomes afraid, leave it for one or two days, do not bind their arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps there will be hot abscesses coming on.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not go into the bath, then reopen the wound if it pleases them.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, or blood flows out subtly and you doubt that it will not be enough for your purpose, then direct all the flame straight into that same opening.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work quickly, rather than waiting for it to swell;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen the wound, and put a little olive oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is helpful in this situation as oil is akin to grease.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the olive oil ointment to each wound you treat in order to staunch the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same effect is created by triacle and bile when applied to the wound.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so subtly does it separate the blood when it has grown too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if it turns into a large abscess, which often happens, especially when bloodletting has not been done recently or the opening of the vein is small, then you should hurry and apply a moist sponge soaked in warm water and salt to the site, compressing it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and afterwards you must do this after the blood has been let from the vein, and if it remains in place for a few days without any blackness or greenness appearing, then it does no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see anything black or green appearing there, apply something made of aloe or myrrh mixed with galbanum juice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there is abscess and appearance of an aperture at the base of the skull:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, then this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid that you put pressure on any part of what we have mentioned, for perhaps it pierces the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But apply a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person's blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it exit until it becomes red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see that it is large, leave it alone until it becomes thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for him who is full and strong, and requires bloodletting, that a wider wound be made for him, and the flames [of the cauterization] should be broad.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it is appropriate to bloodlet often and in small amounts, and one must bloodlet by making a cross-wise cut, not a straight one.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bloodletting is safe from excessive loss of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is better than long or broad bloodletting.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for him whose body is weak after bloodletting, it is appropriate to give him moist bread in the juice of pomegranates.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is overheated, draw three or four times [worth of blood] from him; and if he is of a cold complexion, give him beforehand moist bread in muscatel syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory root, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the treatment, after the loss of much blood, it is necessary that he drinks meat broth, and subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to draw out the arm, and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And for those who wish to draw out the arm after the first bleeding, and have a strong body, they should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And for those who wish to be bled elsewhere, they should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has much blood within his body which is already heated, and causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If it requires extracting a large quantity, and enlarging the opening until it yields with compression;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then you restore all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his pulse as he heals, lest death come in place of compression, and this happens many times when the healers are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not appropriate when you wish to release the arm, and extract blood a second time, while the opening is closed, for you to press heavily upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	Unless it is crooked, have him extend the arm gently, as this would be harmful otherwise.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But leave it until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Where you pierce it with the tip of flame, until the blood that has frozen exits from the wound, and place upon it some lint soaked in water, pressing lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, let it drain from the same place, or another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arm is drained in place of the vein of the head because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of the cautery is such that the patient immerses their hand in hot water until the nails are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then be bound lightly so that the vein appears clearly, then cauterize it now across its width, neither too broad nor too narrow.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And if the wound is large, cauterize it close to where the hand joins the arm, and if blood cannot escape, return the hand to hot water, allowing blood to flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is summer, do not bathe the hand in warm water, as it should be done more often in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as it does not involve an artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding from the vein on the right side of the hand is beneficial for all liver ailments, and this is how it should be done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Immerse the hand in warm water until the vein swells up so it becomes visible.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the bleeding is transverse, and you cut it entirely from end to end, it will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, completely bare of flesh; then immerse the hand in warm water, if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	Once you have extracted as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and lint to the vein in order to seal it; do this for every wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding of the left arm's veins is beneficial for all spleen diseases; do this in the same way as I told you to do on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is valuable for all diseases below the body, such as illnesses of the uterus, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar ailments of the thighs and legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of this medicine are such that the patient puts his foot in warm water and rubs it over the vein until it breaks up, then binds it above the ankle.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And this vein is located at the ankle, and from there it ascends up the leg in many branches.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Treat therefore the largest branch, which is at the ankle, for it moves better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the leg, beware of the nerves which are underneath, and treat it across just as when cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot escape, return the foot to the water and allow the vein to be thoroughly emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it fails to cauterize the first time, repeat the process a second time slightly above, for the area is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and treat the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the back of the ankle, and its evacuation serves to relieve hip pain when caused by hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	The quality of the cauterization is such that the patient should enter a bath and compress above the ankle for four days with twisting, as otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it does open, cauterize thoroughly in all possible ways, crossing the skin.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better to cut it, for the area is dry, and many men are sensitive there.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it [the bone], look for a line on the foot's back or toward the little toe and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	Remove the blood until you see it flowing out, then untie the ligature and apply cotton compresses to hold it in place.
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Cupping incisions.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made of horn, or brass, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is done according to two methods.
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by drawing blood or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this method of dry cupping is also done according to two methods.
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Where there is complete fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and venting, which is done by striking and extracting blood and is carried out in fourteen places of the body, some being entirely in the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and others are in the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	And two more at both sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass below the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And the cupping glasses at both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass on the hips.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the cupping glasses at both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the cupping glasses for both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the cupping glasses for both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And the cupping does not draw any blood, only small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and it will not weaken you at all, as is done with vein-letting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it must not be administered, nor with fire or hot iron, in any illness that arises from overindulgence, until the body is completely emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness we must use cupping, or for habit, then administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and in between during each season;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to have cupping performed, have such a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and with such [people] who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and on the neck, and darkness around the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such [people] who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and spit up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such [people] who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the middle of the month, we instruct them to cup themselves after three hours in the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding of the nostril helps with the cracking noise from the head... that reaches the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body [humours];
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this venting is in place of the phlebotomy of the cerebral vein, and one must not allow those with a cold constitution to use it, or those who have catarrh, as it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, the elderly must not use it, nor those with cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal often become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of forgetting.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The venting in the neck is in place of the phlebotomy of the head and the basilica vein, and for this reason, it helps with narrowing of the chest, and fissures in the channel of the lung, and coughing, and fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be done gently, for if it is too tight, it may cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventouses on the two collarbones are useful for headaches, eye inflammation, and migraines, as well as suffocation, tooth root pain, and it is located at the place of the basilic vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must instruct the patient to extend their hand for measurement, taking care not to cut the artery and avoid excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventouses below the chin are useful for oral diseases, such as gum infections, and similar mouth ailments;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is located at the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The swellings of the shoulders are attributed to ailments caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventouses on the elbows are just as effective as the three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the healer not to make it too perfect, for the flesh is bare of muscle, and beneath lie nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttocks is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases below it. The cupping glass should be large and made of brass, as it needs to draw well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps, if it were too thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	And it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping glasses on the legs heal visibly, for they draw blood from all over the body and are beneficial for old pains of the kidneys, bladder, and womb, and relieve inflammation;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are located at the two sophens (joints) and the two ankles, yet over time they weaken the body, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cup is as follows: first place it on an empty area, suck quickly, and then press down firmly. Move it evenly and do not stop until you see the skin turn red and swollen, revealing the redness of the blood beneath.
