puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then lance (make an incision), and replace the cups. Take care with different body compositions, for some have thick flesh, while others have delicate skin.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to wound only once, creating large openings and deep holes.
et suce legierement.	And suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to thin out the path of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very dense, it is necessary to strike a third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out thick and thin blood, we only stop once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we often restart.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, strike it thoroughly, and finish by piercing the heart suddenly; it is necessary for those with thick skin and hard, narrow veins that you oil their cups with an aperitive and dissolutive substance.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is made with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is for the eyes, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or balsam-oil, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the patient has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied; instead, it must be washed after the fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry juice, or pumpkin water, or china root water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with much moisture, it rises easily with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And for those with excessive swelling, they should be raised using old wine, or juice of spinach, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or something similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and one should not bleed with cups either before or during the bath but an hour or two after it.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and they should not sleep after cupping; it is necessary that he sit up both when the cups are to be applied and while being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is healing is choleric, and if their blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	he must take cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, and lettuce in moderation, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little meat, and pork from castrated animals, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with a cold constitution, take honey syrup, and medium-aged wine that is neither old nor new, eat little, few meats, small birds, and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he cups himself, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is fitting to give some men treacle or musk once before cupping, or after, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be refined, but it is not appropriate for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are placed without injury are those put over the liver, and over the breast, gout, abdomen, buttocks, kidneys, and hip, because these limbs cannot bear injury on their skin, and one should not force it except to draw blood from limb to limb, as we do on breasts when a child is nursing;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put cups on the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the size of the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is gravel or stone, as it extracts by its attractive virtue perhaps the gravel, or empties the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so it does when applied over the liver and spleen in cases of retained flatulence, and these cups are administered empty to suck only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered with fire, and at other times filled with tepid water, as in cases of pleurisy, and the cup is filled in this manner with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two thumbs in width and half a palm in depth, and on its side towards the middle there is a small hole, just enough to insert a needle, and it should be made of copper, soft so as not to injure the patient when applied to the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it has in the middle a bar of copper or iron across which to place a burning candle, and they come in various sizes, both large and small, according to the ailments and the constitution of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For children's cupping glasses are different from those of adults, and those of thin people from those of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus you must apply this cupping glass to the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the candle of wax or linen, and place it inside the cupping glass through the hole that is in the middle of the glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the glass and does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it on the limb, and keep your hands over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, you can release the vapour, and remove the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take the linen again as before, and repeat this often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass used for treating pleurisy, there is no handle or opening and it is applied only when full of water, being placed solely on the affected limb.
et c’est li forme:	and its shape is:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are not applied except to limbs where cupping glasses cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the exposed flesh of the body, such as cheeks or eyelids, and similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	The quality of the suction cups is such that when you find those filled with clean water without sediment, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in lukewarm water for one night until they become soft, ensuring they have no contents in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then proceed with bleeding by opening the vein and using cupping therapy, then massage the limb until it turns red, and apply the poultices.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall off (the poultices), if it is where cupping can be applied, then apply the cupping therapy, for this helps greatly afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, cleanse the area with oil, then water, very well, and afterward dry it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the area bleeds too much after removing the poultices, dampen a linen cloth with cold water and place it on top until the bleeding stops.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is multiplied, apply crushed vitriol on warts or similar things, until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	where you place half of a peeled broad bean, leaving it until it dries up on the spot, so that now it will staunch.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the leeches do not want to attach themselves, rub the spot of fresh blood or prick it with a needle until some blood flows out and then put them on, as soon as they sense the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are defecating, apply a powder of fresh aloe and flax seed or ashes on them, so they will now detach.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu'il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n'en lurent;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason knowledge is strange to our land, as I have never found any good ones.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except for the knowledge from ancient books where I have studied so much that I can treat this science through experience and by habit.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained herein and abridged it at the end, clearly showing the forms of instruments used as I did in these two chapters before this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and remains true to reality, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or breakage occurs in someone, you must hurry to bleed the patient from one side and another if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of body, children, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	Ou si le temps n'est pas très chaud, ou trop froid;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	Et mange des choses froides, comme des salades, du fromage et du chevreuil, et ne bois pas de vin, ni ne mange aucune viande grasse, et ne t'emplisse pas trop de viandes qui remplissent les veines de sang, tant que tu n'as pas peur d'une infection chaude, ou d'un écoulement de matière dans le membre;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Si revient le malade à son premier régime qu'il avait suivi.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, one should nourish the patient with meats that produce thick nourishment and viscosity, such as wheat boiled in water, rice, testicles, feet, calf stomachs, eggs, fresh fish, red wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with too much nourishment, the bones grow quickly and the fracture is more likely to occur again.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Et sachez que les os brisés des vieillards et des décrépits ne peuvent pas être réparés ni soudés correctement selon leur nature à cause du dessèchement des membres, tout comme ceux qui sont trop tendres, tels que les os d'enfants en bas âge;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but have no care, reunite above the broken bone with thick tendons that bind and join the member together, so that it enforces as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not at all leave him from his work, and for this reason he must be nourished with substantial meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that dislocations are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the arm, or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways fractures can occur.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	As there is fracture that goes into splinters, and another in sharpening, like the cutting edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is fracture with an open wound, or fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to each manner have its own tool, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the bone's breakage is known through this, that its place is twisted and clearly appears from outside, and it sounds hollow when pressed by hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting nor hollow sound upon touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is certainly no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can indeed have tortuosity, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that follow here, then hold it firmly and carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes lengthwise, and its two parts are disjoined, it is now necessary to align them evenly, otherwise hot abscesses will arise.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come about, leave them for a day until the abscess is eased.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then align it equally to the muscles that you can feel lightly and gently, and know that its restoration is easier than for those with fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then restrain it as must be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone it is broken into pieces, then stretch it into two parts, whether it be hand or foot, or use one rope for a small limb, or two ropes for a larger member.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you bring them together and reposition all the additions in their places as much as you can, and make sure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the two ends of the bones well according to their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it heals well, do not restrain it too much or press upon it as some do who cause through their work hot abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, you must instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, or in turning over, or any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is secured so firmly that there is no sensation of pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain felt, it is not yet ready, and one must place it in such a position that there is no pain felt.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And take care to ensure that it is correctly aligned so that no crookedness comes about once it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs such as arms and fingers and similar ones.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	One must wrap them in soft, fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those who are overweight, like thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	you should wrap it with a wide and firm bandage, as the broad bands embrace the entire large limb, constricting it evenly from all sides so that there is no pressure.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind it with light padding, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on the bandage, then go above the fracture and loosen it a bit so that the fracture can move away.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and loosen the bandage little by little until you ease much of the healthy part, then take another bandage and bind it again on top of the broken area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the area below the break, and hold it gently, neither too hard nor too softly, as we have said in the first line above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the limbs linen swabs or soft cloth, so that they are all even, then bind it all with bandages above, and then put on your well-made splints, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, apply something to soothe the heat of the abscess, and reduce the swelling, leaving it like this for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then place your splints above, and let them be half the width of a flexible cane that has been cut open, or of the wood used to make shingles, or of palm ribs, and let them be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the star which one places on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as is appropriate for the limb, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on top of the stars just like you did with the first dressing, then tie above it a thread appropriately, as in the first dressing for the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	narrower on top, wider below
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen in the work of some fools who make their dressings with twisted flax cords, this is a great mistake, because the dressing cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have more than two finger-widths between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the head of the shoulder after its restriction in their arm, place beneath it pads made of linen or woolen cloth so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will speak of its cure afterward.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to reset all dislocated limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, one must not insert splints sooner than after 5 days or 7, or more according to your confidence in abscess occurring suddenly.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And take some flour that is found on the mill walls, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; this is the common method of plastering to restore fracture in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster to restore fracture, dislocation, and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Pren saupoudrez d'abréïs et de ladanier, ajoutez l'inule et de l'asafétida; incorporez de la gomme arabique et du muguet, pour un total de 10 mesures.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mélangez de la myrrhe et de l'aloès, pour un total de cinq mesures.
alechil VIIII З.;	Ajoutez huit mesures d'ail.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	Moudre le tout pour faire une poudre et mélanger avec un blanc d'œuf.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the patient's constitution is warm, this plaster can be used as it has a good composition and helps to restore broken bones rapidly for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another type of plaster that is beneficial for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and viscous mallow, take ten and three.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloe, take nine and three;
acaice VI З.;	Wild mint, take six and three;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Armeniaca powder ten and three; grind it well and mix with water or egg white, then administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another plaster for joints and dislocated bones to relieve pain, ease swelling, reduce bone rubbing, and treat fractures.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new wool, boil it in water and oil, then apply to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore the joint or bone to its place, but are good for cooling hot abscesses and properly easing the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another plaster for setting broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves, earth pepper leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another type of poultice for bone fracture repair and to reduce swelling caused by abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take roots of marshmallow, chamomile flowers, violet blossoms, flour of beans, one part each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them together, mix with wine; if the limb is hot, add moist coriander water or plain water and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another poultice method stronger than the first when an abscess has formed in limb repair.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take marshmallow roots, flax seeds, pomegranate flowers, melilot, valerian root, and violet and chamomile blossoms, one part each.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind together and mix with salt water, fresh water or wine depending on the limb's heat and rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on the broken limb to restore it other than a mixture of wax and oil, nothing else, and he says that it must be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen suggests that one should apply dry things slightly warm to the broken limb in order to heal it, such as myrrh, aloe, incense and similar items, as we have mentioned before.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another type of plaster useful for injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and chopped human hair or bird feathers, viscous plant sap, and equal parts leather, grind them all together, make a plaster and let it set.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	Then you let it loosen a little after, making sure the patient feels no pain nor has the bone moved out of place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If not loosened by hand outdoors.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain returns to the spot or itching, with rest or swelling, act fast and loosen it, removing the plaster at once.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	Take light cloth, moist marine sponge, dip it in water and apply to the spot until itching stops and pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb to rest for an hour, then apply dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it onto a nut until you are certain of an abscess heat.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	It will rest the inflammation of the limb, and the pain shall be relieved, then resume the gentle binding, with a little plaster, but do not bind it so tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has softened and turned red, causing pain and swelling which have all been removed, and you need an ointment and bandage, restart it as equally as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if there is no improvement in the limb as we have described, then do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And never release it for twenty days, as we have observed, until the broken part has healed, and approaches proper alignment.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Then hold him more firmly than before, and thicken his flesh, as I have said previously;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot reach it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Bathe it therefore in warm water every time you reset it, and do this every third day, and ease the tension a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this treatment, nourishment is restored to the limb, and corrects the deformity caused by those foolish surgeons who set it crookedly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is evil, and such work is frightening, and I see no other way but to leave it be and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For it has breaks caused by sword impacts, and the shaft removes all the bone down to the marrow that lies beneath the bone, just as an axe or a pole does.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this reason, this type of break is called "axe fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the sword cuts through the bone without penetrating, and this type of break is called "absolute fracture.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And these two types of breaks cause large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or splitting, like from a stone or spearhead, or falling on stones, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is as fine as a hair embedded in the bone, with a small fissure, this break is called "capillary fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is caused by a blow from a stone or by falling or similar, and it drives a fragment of bone into the cavity below, and the skin edges gape like those of a cauldrons when the tinsmith beats upon them.
si entre li piere dedens.	if it drives stone within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this occurs more often in those with moist bones underneath the skin, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it occurs in all these manners of fracture that small fragments become separated, like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures through their displacement, and examination by touch, and through the corrupted flesh on top of them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is understood by this: when you uncover the bone and rub it, the black fracture opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take care of the patient's accidents and symptoms, and if you see no ill accident such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, dizziness, fainting, feverishness, eyes turning pale and reddening, and other similar things in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no dreadful accident and expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, during winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can treat it.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the tissue beneath the bone become corrupted and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the affected part thus.
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And you must take the patient's head and expose the bone in every way possible, revealing the wound as gently as you can, and if there is any bleeding from uncovering the bone or an abscess forms, then provide aid accordingly, for you should fill this place with cloth moistened in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	Let it rest until the hot abscess is relieved, ensuring there is no more bleeding.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin removing it from the bone, this is done in two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One way is to make an incision narrow in front, and this has the following form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have several different kinds of knives, some narrow and others broad, they should be pointed, and made entirely of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly so that you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and solid, you must drill into it instead, rather than using knives and chisels, do not pierce through to the brain, there should be a rim or circle on top of the point, so that the tip does not pass beyond the skull.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you will need several of these, so that each one fits into its place according to the type of bone, and you should have chisels for the entire skull.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three types of arrowheads:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The way to pierce around the broken bone is that you place one arrowhead on top of the bone, and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then move the arrowhead elsewhere slightly afterwards, and do this all around, then use cutters to remove the space of bone between the perforations, doing so as finely and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you extract the bone by hand or with any tools you have such as pincers or pliers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And be careful not to touch the brain nor the soft parts.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	When you have pierced the bone and extracted it, you must clean the cavity left by the bone with any other similar instrument like an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than any other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there is nothing left of the small bones or scales, remove them lightly with one of your instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, it is more safe.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	Strike [the bone] hard, for this is his advice.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture is visible, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place underneath the head of this lenticular chisel, which has such a form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut it on one side only when the other is already acute to the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike gently with a small mallet above it so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and be well aware of the membrane underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhering to the bone, remove it gently, for one removes it easily without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the marrow, and the bone is only cut above, with small pieces remaining, you must smooth this roughness, and remove the splinters with a fine rasp, of which you should have various sizes, to accommodate each place appropriately, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large rasps first, then finer ones, and do not cease until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-trimming incisions or delicate breaks, you must adjust accordingly according to its direction.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something not given in detail by him who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, you must take a piece of linen cloth according to the size of the wound, dip it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another piece of cloth doubled over twice or thrice, and dampen it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the wound, then apply another bandage on top, but do not tighten it too much, only enough to hold the wound in place.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	Leave it like this for one or two days, until the hot abscess is cooled, then untie it and apply medicated poultices such as lily root, oat flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar remedies.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Make a powder from these things and apply it to the wound, then treat with gentle medicated poultices without any harsh binding or pressure.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure the wound is always clean, so as not to leave ointment there or allow pus to accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the brain membrane, it will flow out and cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies corrosive substances onto it, they will corrode from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any mishap occurs to the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackening occurs solely due to the medicine that has been applied there, and this medicine has such a property, then you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil, mix it into a paste, and apply this onto the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it in the manner of treatments that is appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken, or just one, for there are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	The upper one is cartilaginous and does not break but only bends or twists, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the nostril and place the broken piece evenly under your index finger, pushing from the outside until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do this gently, and wait for the patient not to feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and the bones cannot be brought back to their place, you must set it equal with the head of a nail slightly thicker.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two pieces, repeat this process, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after seven or ten days, when the hot abscess is calmed, then put a tent of fine linen cloth on the head of the nose if the fracture is in one place.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you apply another elsewhere if there is a fracture.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the tents be so large that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one should wet the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think it is good, but they must be moistened with a mixture of raw egg white and flour.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent in place until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes goose quills are used in place of tents and a soft cloth is wrapped around them. If the fracture is held in place and the patient breathes into it, it helps the healing process.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Frolick whatever you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form at the nose while you are working on it, apply some softened wax or cotton moistened with rose oil, or put a bit of quicklime there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses don't form there, apply a plaster from the outside, made of bran flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light cotton wool on top, but do not tie it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	If the bone fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose, then cut open the wound, treat the surrounding flesh by cleaning and suturing it, sealing and dressing it with plasters and ointments suitable for such an injury.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, treat it with tenting, and insert splints of plum wood until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	For the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured below, and there is no external wound, and the break is only outside, not broken into two, nor bent inward, it can be identified gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left jawbone, insert your right index finger, and push the fracture gently from inside, shape it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is divided into two, you must administer an extension of both parts until it is aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if there are disturbances or ruptures of the teeth, secure them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then apply wax to the broken jawbone and cover it with a double bandage.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	Cover the bandage with a well-made large splint or an equal-sized piece of leather that is long and wide according to the jawbone's length, secure it as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest and consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the alignment changes, dislocate it on the third day, then reset to what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply a plaster on top, made with mill powder and an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the scabs.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put a light woolen plaster on top, and if the plaster hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a warm abscess appears, apply what we have mentioned many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture with an accompanying wound, first ensure that no part of the bone has been removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	So subtly to remove the instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and no more remain, cleanse the wound if it is wide; apply appropriate dressings to generate flesh until it heals.
de la forcele	Of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forearm breaks multiple times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or it is broken and split into two, with pieces, and this is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the treatment is as follows when the fracture is without a wound: have two assistants so that one can hold the arm where it is broken.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	While the other extends the neck towards the affected part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then align the fracture with your two hands so that it fits together properly, without any displacement or unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need more extension, place beneath the patient's shoulder a round pad of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	extend the arm and lift it up, hold the pad firmly in your hand, so that you can align the break properly as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull out the head of the broken limb from without because it has gone in perfectly, then have the patient lie prone on their back and place a medium-sized pillow under his shoulder; have your assistants push down on the shoulder until the bone of the fractured area is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then direct the broken part towards your hands, and if you find it shattered, you must split it upwards.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw the pieces gently together, and if the bone cannot join despite all attempts at elevation, then cut it with one of your knives.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place beneath the arm this instrument to protect the skin.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, it is not wood, and it should also be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two edges, as you can see, and one edge should be wide, while the other is narrow, just like the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, cut open the wound, and if the opening is small or you suspect a deep-seated abscess, pack the wound with lint and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess appears, dampen a cloth with rose oil, egg white, and wine, then apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The immobilization of the bone when there is no fracture or injury involves applying a poultice of mill powder and egg white onto the bone, followed by light dressings on top. Place a cushion underneath if needed to support it during this process.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage, one palm-width across, then place two layers of cloth over the wool and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that one end of the bandage hangs free.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	Place the stick on the fracture, then wrap the bandage around the neck and under both armpits.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And pull on each end of the bandage until you see that it holds the fracture in place and the stick doesn't move over the broken bone. Loosen the ties daily but retighten them if they become slack.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on their back, placing a small pillow under their neck when they sleep to raise the shoulder upward.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If it alleviates the fracture's pain by aligning the shoulder, bind their arm to their neck, and do not release them for twenty days unless an unfortunate accident occurs.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then reapply the poultice if you see that it is necessary, restraining them and leaving them in this manner until they are restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And she will be healed within twenty-eight days at most, and in less time for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	For a broken shoulder.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Sometimes the shoulder dislocates or moves out of place at its joint, not from force but merely by being touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If you align it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then place on it some flour from the mill with an egg white, and light pads, and put a double cloth over it.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on top a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint slips off anywhere around the shoulder, then use linen pads to secure it so that the splint sits evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then secure it firmly with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time he moves, hold it fast, and set the sternum straight if it has shifted from its place, and let the patient lie on their affected side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is complete, untie him, and be confident, for it is not a bone that can be easily dislocated.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts forward and punctures beneath the heart, do so above it, remove it, and follow what we have said for treating abscess-causing fractures.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the spine
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The foot is sometimes broken in half, but this rarely happens.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks above (the ankle).
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it slants downwards and the patient feels great pain, lacks movement, and coughs; they may also vomit blood, and the broken ends of bone are clearly seen through the skin, which is easily felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration method is to have the patient lie often on their back, and place a cushion between their shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and bring the sides of the two collarbones together with your hands, and subtly adjust as needed in every way you can, until the bone's shape is correct.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place on plasters and swabs above a slender stalk of salt, or some other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, binding it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	Tie the bandage around in a circle at the back, and tighten it appropriately, then undo it every hour to check if it has softened, tightening it again if so.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	If it needs to be unbound due to corrosion or itching in the area, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, remove the plaster, and address the issue with appropriate treatment methods.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reapply the plaster and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that rib fractures only occur in the back and on the chest side towards the spine, and also inside near the head, as they are brittle bones.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And it is felt well when pressing on the affected area during examination of the ribs.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a plaster cast, and secure it with a splint if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is pushed inward, the patient feels severe pain and a pricking sensation like pins and needles because the bone is piercing the tissue.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	They breathe rapidly and suffer from acute pain as well as violent coughing and vomiting of large quantities of blood; it is a serious illness which ancient physicians tried to treat with great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And so there are some who say one must administer meats that swell the belly to push the rupture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not cause this [condition], if hot abscesses have not come there already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, treat them with cauterization.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	Some said to place cups over the affected area for suction which seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw out excesses from their place due to the condition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say to cover the spot with wet wool in hot oil, and put tent-like wrappings between the ribs to make even the tension around [the wound], then treat it with treatment for pleurisy, meat broth, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone piercing the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient's mind, then it is necessary to make an incision over the location of the broken rib, and one must place beneath it a tool to protect the soft tissue.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	one must then cut the bone and gently extract it, and thereafter sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an inflamed abscess forms, place damp linen cloths soaked in rose oil over the location.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat it while it is still soft at this time that suits the abscess, and let it lie constantly on its side where it must be until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	From the broken neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is breakage of the bones in the neck, and this often happens when it bends.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note: if their hands become soft, swollen, and numb, unable to move or extend, and when you prick them with a needle, they feel no pain.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many cases, but if they can change position and feel well when pressed or pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and the patient may be cured with proper treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healed or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if there are any accidents that occur when they are in hand, and on the back watch out for windiness and egestion without volition;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when they lie softened on their belly, there should be egestion without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back and he wants to mount [a horse], he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	He knows they are deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If you do not work on his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not befall him, then the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is such that you reward him if there is hot abscess, apply rosin oil or fresh egg yolk until it subsides.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And let him not sleep on that part of his body where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes dislocated, you must cut into the heart above it.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, and treat it with ointment to promote healing until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone of the shoulder is broken, which is called the "collarbone", place your left palm on it and push, aligning it with the other hand, then apply a poultice and a bandage over it, if necessary.
